	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Boundary (topology)</span></h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">All points not part of the interior of a subset of a topological space</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about boundaries in general topology. It is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Boundary_of_a_manifold" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary of a manifold">boundary of a manifold</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boundary_of_a_locally_closed_subset" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary of a locally closed subset">boundary of a locally closed subset</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-More_footnotes plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-More_footnotes" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article includes a list of general <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">references</a>, but <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Runge_theorem.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Runge_theorem.svg/220px-Runge_theorem.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Runge_theorem.svg/330px-Runge_theorem.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Runge_theorem.svg/440px-Runge_theorem.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Runge_theorem.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A set (in light blue) and its boundary (in dark blue).</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> in general, the <b>boundary</b> of a subset <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> of a <a href="/wiki/Topological_space" title="Topological space">topological space</a> <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">X</span> is the set of points in the <a href="/wiki/Closure_(topology)" title="Closure (topology)">closure</a> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> not belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Interior_(topology)" title="Interior (topology)">interior</a> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>. An element of the boundary of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is called a <b>boundary point</b> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>. The term <b>boundary operation</b> refers to finding or taking the boundary of a set.  Notations used for boundary of a set <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> include <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \operatorname {bd} (S),\operatorname {fr} (S),}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>bd</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>fr</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \operatorname {bd} (S),\operatorname {fr} (S),}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/76f1bb953501c11dfda19f46552eb4d7866c4278" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.506ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \operatorname {bd} (S),\operatorname {fr} (S),}"/></span>  and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \partial S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c609f4d3c5692ea4495479ef47594dc67f9fa464" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.817ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\partial S"/></span>.  Some authors (for example Willard, in <i>General Topology</i>) use the term <b>frontier</b> instead of boundary in an attempt to avoid confusion with a <a href="/wiki/Manifold#Manifold_with_boundary" title="Manifold">different definition</a> used in <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_topology" title="Algebraic topology">algebraic topology</a> and the theory of <a href="/wiki/Manifold" title="Manifold">manifolds</a>.  Despite widespread acceptance of the meaning of the terms boundary and frontier, they have sometimes been used to refer to other sets.  For example, <i>Metric Spaces</i> by E. T. Copson uses the term boundary to refer to <a href="/wiki/Felix_Hausdorff" title="Felix Hausdorff">Hausdorff</a>'s <b>border</b>, which is defined as the intersection of a set with its boundary.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Hausdorff also introduced the term <b>residue</b>, which is defined as the intersection of a set with the closure of the border of its complement.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Connected_space#Formal_definition" title="Connected space">connected component</a> of the boundary of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span> is called a <b>boundary component</b> of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">S</span>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Common_definitions">Common definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Common definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are several equivalent definitions for the <em>boundary</em> of a subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S\subseteq X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>&#x2286;<!-- ⊆ --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S\subseteq X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/44aba72977e43f863dd873b095d1dc0bd3f17608" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:6.578ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="S\subseteq X"/></span> of a topological space <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X,}">
  <semantics>

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09ba32eeb405f7f5f2bac1eb12987c47d2fd42df" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.627ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="X,"/></span> which will be denoted by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>Bd</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>

<p>A <em>boundary point</em> of a set refers to any element of that set's boundary. The boundary <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7ed60827917abec164aa44fe529d368421a106a9" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.366ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S}"/></span> defined above is sometimes called the set's <em>topological boundary</em> to distinguish it from other similarly named notions such as <a href="/wiki/Boundary_of_a_manifold" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary of a manifold">the boundary</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Manifold_with_boundary" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifold with boundary">manifold with boundary</a> or the boundary of a <a href="/wiki/Manifold_with_corners" class="mw-redirect" title="Manifold with corners">manifold with corners</a>, to name just a few examples.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The closure of a set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> equals the union of the set with its boundary: 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\overline {S}}=S\cup \partial _{X}S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mover>
            <mi>S</mi>
            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
          </mover>
        </mrow>

where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\overline {S}}=\operatorname {cl} _{X}S}">

A set is closed if and only if it contains its boundary, and open if and only if it is disjoint from its boundary. The boundary of a set is <a href="/wiki/Closed_set" title="Closed set">closed</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> this follows from the formula <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S~:=~{\overline {S}}\cap {\overline {(X\setminus S)}},}">

</p><p>("Trichotomy")<span class="anchor" id="Trichotomy"></span> Given any subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S\subseteq X,}">

Consequently, if these set are not empty<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> then they form a <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_a_set" title="Partition of a set">partition</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X.}">

</p><p>A point <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p\in X}">

        <mi>p</mi>
        <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p\in X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fae5d7ae3f7710fc989d0bd6dca038d74107f16d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:6.08ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="p\in X"/></span> is a boundary point of a set if and only if every neighborhood of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle p}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>p</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;" alt="p"/></span> contains at least one point in the set and at least one point not in the set. 
The boundary of the interior of a set as well as the boundary of the closure of a set are both contained in the boundary of the set.

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3500d05a8f761313103968e3942c4ed235f88135" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.217ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="B="/></span> set of <b>boundary points</b> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e0bcd8516b165aaacb234616d7d2d23478a35be7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.146ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="S,"/></span> area shaded green = set of <a href="/wiki/Interior_point" class="mw-redirect" title="Interior point">interior points</a> of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S,}">

  <semantics>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e0bcd8516b165aaacb234616d7d2d23478a35be7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.146ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="S,"/></span> areas shaded black = empty sets.  Every point of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>

      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> is either an interior point or a boundary point.  Also, every point of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> is either an accumulation point or an isolated point.  Likewise, every boundary point of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> is either an accumulation point or an isolated point.  Isolated points are always boundary points.</i>
</p>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characterizations_and_general_examples">Characterizations and general examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Characterizations and general examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The boundary of a set is equal to the boundary of the set's complement: 
<div class="mwe-math-element"><div class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S=\partial _{X}(X\setminus S).}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo class="MJX-variant">&#x2216;<!-- ∖ --></mo>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S=\partial _{X}(X\setminus S).}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></div><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/628741399fe902ed9da0cfb3cb4f8d9f14c2474c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:18.461ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}S=\partial _{X}(X\setminus S).}"/></div>
</p><p>A set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle U}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>U</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle U}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/458a728f53b9a0274f059cd695e067c430956025" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.783ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="U"/></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Dense_subset" class="mw-redirect" title="Dense subset">dense</a> <a href="/wiki/Open_set" title="Open set">open</a> subset of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="X"/></span> if and only if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}U=X\setminus U.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo class="MJX-variant">&#x2216;<!-- ∖ --></mo>
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \partial _{X}U=X\setminus U.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a12bc16ed0b96f4c968314ef5e94e716c00df4c3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.352ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \partial _{X}U=X\setminus U.}"/></span> 
</p><p>The interior of the boundary of a closed set is the empty set.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;proof 1&#93;</a></sup> 
Consequently, the interior of the boundary of the closure of a set is the empty set. 
The interior of the boundary of an open set is also the empty set.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;proof 2&#93;</a></sup> 
Consequently, the interior of the boundary of the interior of a set is the empty set. 
In particular, if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S\subseteq X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>&#x2286;<!-- ⊆ --></mo>
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S\subseteq X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/44aba72977e43f863dd873b095d1dc0bd3f17608" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:6.578ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="S\subseteq X"/></span> is a closed or open subset of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/68baa052181f707c662844a465bfeeb135e82bab" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.98ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="X"/></span> then there does not exist any non-empty subset <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle U\subseteq \partial _{X}S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>U</mi>
        <mo>&#x2286;<!-- ⊆ --></mo>
        <msub>
          <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>X</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle U\subseteq \partial _{X}S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dab37911fe6a305fd7566e679e9ffd4f7ab0f2d7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.247ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle U\subseteq \partial _{X}S}"/></span> such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle U}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>U</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle U}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/458a728f53b9a0274f059cd695e067c430956025" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.783ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="U"/></span> is also an open subset of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle X.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>X</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle X.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5ba76c5a460c4a0bb1639a193bc1830f0a773e03" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.627ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="X."/></span> 
This fact is important for the definition and use of <a href="/wiki/Nowhere_dense_set" title="Nowhere dense set">nowhere dense subsets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meager_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Meager set">meager subsets</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Baire_space" title="Baire space">Baire spaces</a>. 
</p><p>A set is the boundary of some open set if and only if it is closed and <a href="/wiki/Nowhere_dense_set" title="Nowhere dense set">nowhere dense</a>. 
The boundary of a set is empty if and only if the set is both closed and open (that is, a <a href="/wiki/Clopen_set" title="Clopen set">clopen set</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concrete_examples">Concrete examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Concrete examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandelbrot_Components.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mandelbrot_Components.svg/220px-Mandelbrot_Components.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mandelbrot_Components.svg/330px-Mandelbrot_Components.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mandelbrot_Components.svg/440px-Mandelbrot_Components.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mandelbrot_Components.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boundary of hyperbolic components of <a href="/wiki/Mandelbrot_set" title="Mandelbrot set">Mandelbrot set</a></div></div></div>
<p>Consider the real line <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

          <mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/786849c765da7a84dbc3cce43e96aad58a5868dc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.678ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\mathbb {R} "/></span> with the usual topology (that is, the topology whose <a href="/wiki/Basis_(topology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Basis (topology)">basis sets</a> are <a href="/wiki/Open_interval" class="mw-redirect" title="Open interval">open intervals</a>) and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {Q} ,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mi mathvariant="double-struck">Q</mi>
        </mrow>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>

</p>
<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial (0,5)=\partial [0,5)=\partial (0,5]=\partial [0,5]=\{0,5\}}">

<li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial \varnothing =\varnothing }">

<p>These last two examples illustrate the fact that the boundary of a <a href="/wiki/Dense_set" title="Dense set">dense set</a> with empty interior is its closure. They also show that it is possible for the boundary <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial S}">

    </mrow>

</p><p>The boundary of a set is a <a href="/wiki/Topology" title="Topology">topological</a> notion and may change if one changes the topology.  For example, given the usual topology on <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \mathbb {R} ^{2},}">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundary_of_an_open_ball_vs._its_surrounding_sphere">Boundary of an open ball vs. its surrounding sphere</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Boundary of an open ball vs. its surrounding sphere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This example demonstrates that the topological boundary of an open ball of radius <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle r&gt;0}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>r</mi>
        <mo>&gt;</mo>
        <mn>0</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r&gt;0}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23cbbcd53bd13620bc53490e3eec42790850b452" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:5.31ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="r &gt; 0"/></span> is <em>not</em> necessarily equal to the corresponding sphere of radius <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle r}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>r</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="r"/></span> (centered at the same point); it also shows that the closure of an open ball of radius <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle r&gt;0}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>r</mi>
        <mo>&gt;</mo>
        <mn>0</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundary_of_a_boundary">Boundary of a boundary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boundary_(topology)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Boundary of a boundary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For any set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S,\partial S\supseteq \partial \partial S,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>&#x2287;<!-- ⊇ --></mo>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S,\partial S\supseteq \partial \partial S,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5e881f0f0ab7405497b69d67898f05fa1728ef0a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.231ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle S,\partial S\supseteq \partial \partial S,}"/></span> where <a href="/wiki/List_of_mathematical_symbols_by_subject#Set_relations" title="List of mathematical symbols by subject"><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \,\supseteq \,}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mo>&#x2287;<!-- ⊇ --></mo>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \,\supseteq \,}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d6b0a683c276de4f94c4cc36590ecdefd9d56e2b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:2.582ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \,\supseteq \,}"/></span></a> denotes the <a href="/wiki/Superset" class="mw-redirect" title="Superset">superset</a> with equality holding if and only if the boundary of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> has no interior points, which will be the case for example if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4611d85173cd3b508e67077d4a1252c9c05abca2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.499ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S"/></span> is either closed or open.  Since the boundary of a set is closed, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \partial \partial S=\partial \partial \partial S}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x2202;<!-- ∂ --></mi>
        <mi>S</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \partial \partial S=\partial \partial \partial S}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c0bdfddcefd8a00692ddaef33fcecc80b04d3e00" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:12.687ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \partial \partial S=\partial \partial \partial S}"/></span> for any set <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle S.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>S</mi>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle S.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23bbb1f0f6ebdfa78b4fed06049640f7386bb44b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.146ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="S."/></span>  The boundary operator thus satisfies a weakened kind of <a href="/wiki/Idempotence" title="Idempotence">idempotence</a>.
</p><p>In discussing boundaries of <a href="/wiki/Manifold" title="Manifold">manifolds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Simplex" title="Simplex">simplexes</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Simplicial_complex" title="Simplicial complex">simplicial complexes</a>, one often meets the assertion that the boundary of the boundary is always empty.  Indeed, the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Singular_homology" title="Singular homology">singular homology</a> rests critically on this fact.  The explanation for the apparent incongruity is that the topological boundary (the subject of this article) is a slightly different concept from the boundary of a manifold or of a simplicial complex.  For example, the boundary of an open disk viewed as a manifold is empty, as is its topological boundary viewed as a subset of itself, while its topological boundary viewed as a subset of the real plane is the circle surrounding the disk.  Conversely, the boundary of a closed disk viewed as a manifold is the bounding circle, as is its topological boundary viewed as a subset of the real plane, while its topological boundary viewed as a subset of itself is empty.  In particular, the topological boundary depends on the ambient space, while the boundary of a manifold is invariant.
</p>
